Since the September 18th Incident, our army has vowed to resist to the death and has won every battle. In total, we have fought more than eighty battles of all sizes. All the cities and towns occupied have been immediately handed over to the Self-Defense Army for management after their recovery. Our army spends its nights in the open air and eats in the wind in remote mountains, specializing in attacking and never asking about taxation. Currently, we are gathering all our strength to capture Jilin Province, but the enemy's supplies are sufficient and their weapons are strong. In addition, with air cover, it is extremely difficult for us to succeed. We have already seriously surrounded it, and the complete recovery of the provincial capital is just around the corner, and there is no fear of failure. We have not relaxed our plans to disrupt the railways. Earlier, the Japanese army sent troops to protect the railway and transport lumberjacks to repair the Jidun line for the purpose of a long-term invasion. After our side detected this, we took the lead and Wu Yicheng led troops to intercept the enemy army. After a long battle, we finally defeated the Japanese railway protection army, killing hundreds of enemies and seizing countless supplies of gunpowder, such as machine guns, mortars, and large-caliber guns, as well as bullets. Our army suffered fifty or sixty casualties, and the enemy suffered about two hundred casualties. On the evening of the 14th, our 16th Regiment ambushed the invaders at Baligang, eight miles east of Hengdaohezi, causing the train to derail. The Japanese slaves fled in droves, killing two enemy officers and eight soldiers on the spot, and wounding twelve. Our side also suffered three deaths and six injuries. At that time, our Deputy Commander Kong Xianrong was planning to attack Ning'an County, and the situation was critical. It happened that a large number of gasoline and lumber vehicles were speeding west from the Shala River Station. Deputy Commander Kong heard the news and immediately sent a team to fire missiles, causing the gasoline to ignite and spread to all the enemy's forces. The sound of the explosion was like thunder, and the red flames covered the sky. All the violent Japanese vehicles were reduced to ashes. After suffering this heavy blow, the enemy's railway tracks were completely destroyed, and the rear support became more and more delayed. In the battle of Ning'an, our army killed more than two hundred enemy soldiers. In just half a month, we successively recovered Ning'an County, Tokyo Town, and Hailin Station. The markets and businesses were operating as usual, the schools were reading, the neighborhoods were peaceful, and the soldiers were rejoicing. There were originally three flour mills in Ning'an, two of which were burned down by our army, leaving only the Zengxing Flour Mill to replenish our army's military rations and flour. Although there are scattered Japanese troops hiding near the city, the number is small and it is not difficult to eliminate them with a thorough search. The retreating army has fled in two directions, one retreating to Hailin Station and the other fleeing to the West Mountain. As for ammunition, Commander Wang's arsenal has two hundred workers who manufacture various guns, cannons, and bullets. All are extremely useful. Various empty shell casings are transported back from the front line for reloading and re-sent to the front line for secondary bombardment, which saves time and speed. The clothing factory has fifty workers, but it has not been able to expand its operations due to financial constraints. How can a large amount of medicinal materials be prepared from Guannei so that they can be manufactured continuously? This is what Commander Wang urgently hopes to report to the authorities for attention. The clothing is one item. Because the war zone of our army is located in the extreme border, the weather in the severe winter is colder than elsewhere, and there is already snow and ice on the road. During the recent attack on Ning'an, many soldiers still went into battle wearing only single-layer clothing, and their skin was chapped, which is extremely worrying. In addition, Commander Wang is determined not to disturb the people and merchants, and takes the people as the oath of the army, which is indeed very different from other armies that can raise money on the spot to plan for a full stomach. This is also what the people of Northeast China have seen and heard together. If 70,000 armed comrades are trapped in the icy and snowy land and we do not urgently appeal to all parties for special maintenance and prompt allocation of funds for cotton-padded clothes, trousers, and leather hats, it will be difficult to achieve the final success. This is what Commander Wang urgently hopes to report to the authorities for attention. Secondly, when Decheng was about to leave, the Japanese had not yet completed the Mudanjiang Bridge. When asked about the recent situation of the army, they said that since Zhu Jiqing left the customs this spring to advocate the formation of the Northeast National Salvation Army, the people in various places have risen up to respond and the momentum has grown. They have fought with the Japanese army many times and have achieved considerable victories, but due to insufficient materials, they have not been able to make full progress. In the summer, there were more infantry due to the green gauze tent, but now most of them have been formed into cavalry after the autumn. Currently, there are more cavalry than infantry. Japanese Navy Transferred Back Home

Pay Attention to Sugisaka's Instructions

Commander's Instructions The Shanghai Japanese Naval Landing Force was transferred from Sasebo with 625 new soldiers, of which 240 were assigned to various ships on the Yangtze River, and the remainder were assigned to the Landing Force to supplement the 300 naval personnel who were to be transferred back to Japan. Yesterday morning at 9:00 a.m., they were gathered in the headquarters by Rear Admiral Sugisaka, commander of the Landing Force, to give instructions.

Boarding the Ship to Leave Shanghai After Sugisaka finished his instructions, all the Landing Force soldiers went to the Osaka Wharf to board the special service ship Todoh Maru, which is scheduled to depart from Shanghai at 6:00 a.m. this morning via Wusong and return directly to the Sasebo Naval Base in Japan. Yesterday, many Japanese expatriates in Shanghai went to Yangshupu to see off the army returning home. Commander Sugisaka, Chief of Staff Kajishima, and others also went to the pier to see them off.

Izumo Moves Berth Lieutenant General Sakonji, Commander of the Third Fleet of the Japanese Navy, has now received orders to be promoted to Commander of the Sasebo Naval Port, and Lieutenant General Takahashi will succeed him as Commander of the Third Fleet. Sakonji is preparing to hand over his duties and will leave for home as soon as the new commander arrives. The flagship Izumo of the Third Fleet, which was originally moored at the Nikko Wharf near the Waitanyuan Bridge, moved to the Jiangmian No. 7 and No. 8 river piers in Yangshupu at noon yesterday because the naval soldiers in the ship were being replaced by new ones, so it was moved there to facilitate the boarding and alighting of the soldiers.

Englishman Webb to Fly Home from Shanghai

The Continental News reports that Englishman Webb bought an airplane at an auction house in Shanghai yesterday. If it can be used for long-distance flights after a test flight and is permitted by the government, he plans to fly back to his country in three or four weeks. Webb served in the British Air Force for two years after the European War, and then tried planting rubber trees in the Malay Peninsula for several years. He came to China two years ago and recently operated shipping in the Songhua River, but was squeezed out by the Japanese. He then came south to Shanghai. A few days ago, he happened to see two German-made biplanes for sale in the auction advertisement column in the newspaper, so he bought one for 750 yuan yesterday. The other one was bought by a Chinese aviator for 250 taels. After purchasing the plane, Webb decided to fly back to his country and applied to the government for permission to depart from Hongqiao Airport and reach Hong Kong via Fuzhou and Xiamen. After arriving in Hong Kong, he plans to take the route through Singapore, India, and Egypt to return to England. The aircraft is a Schwalbe two-seater model equipped with a 120-horsepower Siemens engine. It was shipped to Hong Kong four years ago by a certain company, which originally planned to sell it to the government. However, due to the company's liquidation, it was put up for auction, so the aircraft has not been used.

News from the Inspection Group of Disaster Areas in Henan, Anhui, and Hubei

Scheduled to Depart on the 20th

Twenty People in Each Province

The three provinces of Henan, Anhui, and Hubei have long suffered from the ravages of bandits and communists. Since June of this year, the Central Government ordered a general suppression, and Chairman Chiang Kai-shek personally went to Hubei Province to supervise the military operations. Now the military has achieved successive victories, and the bandit areas have been gradually recovered. However, the people are displaced, and the fields and houses are in ruins. The disaster situation is dire and the famine is worrying. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, deeply saddened, specifically telegraphed Mr. Wang Xiaolai to Wuhan, and also telegraphed Mayor Wu and leaders from all walks of life to find ways to provide relief and welcome the organization of an inspection group to go to the three provinces to inspect and understand the true situation of the disaster. Mayor Wu and others specially hosted a banquet for leaders from all walks of life at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce on the evening of the 5th to discuss relief measures. An ad hoc Joint Relief Association for the three provinces of Henan, Anhui, and Hubei was established on the spot. Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Wen Lanting, Zhao Jinqing, Liu Zhanen, Huang Hanzhi, Ye Gongchuo, Yu Xiji, Pan Gongzhan, and other nine people were appointed as preparatory committee members for the inspection group of the three provinces. A committee was set up in the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to welcome various Shanghai organizations and the press to participate in the inspection. According to Mayor Wu's words to the Central News Agency reporter yesterday, the inspection group of disaster areas in Henan, Anhui, and Hubei has been scheduled to depart on the 20th of this month, with a stipulation of twenty people in each province. All round-trip expenses will be borne by the inspectors themselves. However, the respective provincial governments will be responsible for the protection and reception after arriving in the disaster areas.

The Post-Disaster Relief Society for the Jiangwan Disaster Area Decides on Three Measures

This spring, the villages in the Jiangwan area suffered tremendous disasters during the Songhu Anti-Japanese War. The fields and village houses were almost completely burned down. After the end of the war, many civilians were left homeless. The Shanghai Citizens' Local Maintenance Association had successively donated huge sums of money, designating various districts to build memorial villages for the displaced people to live in. The Jiangwan area received 60,000 yuan, and the Municipal Committee of the district planned to build four memorial villages. One village at Gaojing Temple has already been completed, but the villagers are petitioning the Municipal Council because they are not suited to living together due to farming. This is about to cause trouble. In view of this, all parties are urgently planning post-disaster measures to remedy the situation. It was learned yesterday that the Relief Group of the Shanghai War Zone Rehabilitation Committee specially convened a meeting to discuss this matter and decided on three measures on the spot: ㈠ Please transfer the remaining 21,000 yuan of relief funds allocated to the Jiangwan area by the former Local Maintenance Association to relief funds; ㈡ The 15,000 yuan housing loan that the War Zone Rehabilitation Committee should allocate to the Jiangwan area will be allocated as soon as possible; ㈢ The War Zone Rehabilitation Committee will send a letter to the Songhu War Zone Rehabilitation Committee to continue to allocate 100,000 yuan of the second phase of relief funds, which will be submitted by the Social Affairs Bureau to the Municipal Government for review. If the Municipal Government deems it feasible, it will be handled accordingly.

The Shandong Association Cables to Request Not to Deploy Large Troops to Shandong

The Shanghai Shandong Association sent a cable to the military authorities, saying: To Commander Chiang in Hankou, Acting Commander Zhang in Peiping, and Minister He in Nanjing: Upon investigation, the conflict between Han and Liu in Jiaodong has suddenly spanned a month, and the local area is in a state of devastation and misery that is difficult to describe. I have recently seen reports that you have repeatedly ordered a ceasefire, with each side returning to its own defense and that various measures, including the transfer of Liu away from Shandong, are about to be implemented step by step. In this way, the scourge of war will cease and the disputes will be resolved. It can be seen that you are concerned about the national crisis and care about the people. The people of Shandong are overjoyed. However, Jiaodong is located in a strategic location, with neighbors surrounding it to the east. If a gap appears, they will immediately take advantage of it. In order to punish the past and prevent future troubles, after Liu's army leaves Shandong, it is hoped that large troops will not be deployed. Internally, this will avoid conflicts of authority; externally, there will be no grounds for slander. The people's plight will be alleviated and the supply will be slightly restored. This is a natural cause and effect. Therefore, I dare to cable a request to comply with public opinion and not station large troops in the Jiaodong area in the future to avoid disputes and alleviate the people's suffering. The situation is extremely urgent and awaits orders. The Shandong Association in Shanghai bows respectfully.

Assassination Case at the Old North Gate Last Night

A Western-Suited Youth Named Zhang Zhigang

Was Riding a Rickshaw on Yanhai Street

When He Was Shot Three Times and Died on the Spot

At around 8 o'clock last night, a young man of about twenty years old, wearing a Western suit, was riding in a rickshaw near Heng Street, Old North Gate, when suddenly a thug dressed in black shirt and trousers jumped out from the roadside, caught up with the rickshaw, and took out a pistol, firing three shots at the youth in the rickshaw. All three shots hit the youth in the head. The youth fell out of the rickshaw and collapsed on the roadside, bleeding profusely. Passers-by and police officers gathered upon hearing the sound. The youth died on the spot. The police officers immediately reported to the head of the First Sub-station of the Second District by telephone. Upon hearing the news, the head of the sub-station immediately dispatched a patrol officer with armed police officers to round up the suspect, but the murderer had already escaped. The police officers then carefully examined the body of the deceased. They found the three characters "Zhang Zhigang" woven in red velvet inside the lining of the suit coat, and a card in the pocket with "Lu Jinxiang" and "Qinchuan" written on it, followed by "Far East Coal Ball Company Telephone 10669." The patrol officers then took the card and went to the Far East Coal Ball Company to inquire, but the company said that the deceased was not Lu Jinxiang and that they had never heard of Zhang Zhigang. At that time, two five-yuan banknotes and a double-dime silver coin were also found in the deceased's pocket, and there were tattoos on both arms. After half an hour, the First Sub-station of the Second District had completely investigated the deceased's history. The deceased's name was indeed Zhang Zhigang, 29 years old, from Zhenjiang. He had been a gangster in Shanghai for many years and had been sentenced to one year in prison. He had just been released this year. It was also heard that the deceased's wife had come to Shanghai from Zhenjiang the day before yesterday and was staying at the home of a friend, Weng Lao Si. Last night, the deceased also had dinner with his wife at Weng's house before going out alone to visit a friend in the Chinese area of Nanshi. Unexpectedly, he was ambushed by thugs on the way. The body was temporarily placed by the roadside pending an autopsy by the local court today.

Eighty Pieces of Antiquities from the Tongzhou Museum Recovered

Original Stolen Goods Found in the Nankang Hotel

Four People Detained, Wang Er Still Needs to be Apprehended

On the 5th of this month, the Tongzhou Museum suddenly reported a theft, with a total loss of more than 80 pieces of bronze, porcelain, jade, stone and other antique items, all of which were priceless treasures. The authorities immediately conducted investigations everywhere, but there was no trace. At around 8 o'clock yesterday morning, Guan Qu, the head of the First District of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, suddenly received a secret report that the main culprit and stolen goods had sneaked into Shanghai the day before yesterday. He immediately dispatched patrol officer Guo Jifen to lead police chief Pang Zilin and others to inspect various hotels. When they passed the Nankang Hotel on the Bund of the Sixteenth Wharf, they entered to inspect the guests. Not long after, they checked room number four and saw two beds in the room. A man was sleeping on one bed, and another man and woman were sleeping together on the other bed. None of them got up. They immediately stepped forward and ordered them to get up and questioned their backgrounds. One man claimed to be Chen Jinbiao, and the woman (referring to the female guest) was Ms. Chen Xie, whom he did not know. They had only met on the ship. Since they were just meeting for the first time, why were they sleeping together in the same bed? Suspecting the situation, they immediately detained the two. When questioned further, another man claimed to be Zhou Jinquan, but his words were hesitant and his expression was flustered. They were also detained. Afterwards, they conducted a detailed search of the room and found a huge wooden box under the bed. When they opened it, they saw that it contained the eighty-odd pieces of antiques that had been stolen from the Tongzhou Museum recently. The witnesses were taken back to the district office, and police were stationed in the room to wait for the arrest of the remaining accomplices. As expected, another man named Hu Zixiang came to visit not long after and was detained. After being taken to the district office, the district chief, together with the acting officers, arrested Hu Zixiang and others for preliminary interrogation. Chen Jinbiao confessed that he was 34 years old, from Nantong, and had been engaged in the firecracker business. Zhou Jinquan confessed that he was 47 years old, from Nantong. Hu Zixiang confessed that he was 42 years old and from the same hometown as Chen and Zhou. Regarding the origin of the recovered antiques, they all claimed that a man named Wang Er, whom they knew in Nantong a few days ago, had entrusted them with the wooden box to bring to Shanghai on his behalf. Before leaving, he instructed them to be extra careful with the box along the way because it contained valuable items. In order to avoid attention, they took a boat to Haimen, while Wang Er himself took a boat from Tongzhou to wait in Shanghai, meeting at the Yuebin Hotel in Xiaodongmen. If things were successful, they would each be given 15 yuan. Wang Er lived in the Ximen Head Archway area of Tongzhou and used the alias Yu Yi Wu when he came to Shanghai this time. Unexpectedly, they were arrested by the police this morning after taking a boat from Haimen to Shanghai and staying at the Nankang Hotel. As for the detailed origin of the antiques, they really didn't know, etc. When Ms. Chen Xie was questioned, she confessed that she was 32 years old, from Haimen, and had come to Shanghai from her hometown by boat for important matters. She met Chen and others on the ship. When the ship arrived at the dock last night, it was already late, so Chen and others invited her to stay at the Nankang Hotel. At first, she slept alone in one bed, but Chen suddenly climbed onto her bed in the middle of the night and slept with her under the same quilt. She was caught by the police this morning, but she knew nothing about the antiques, etc. The police were then dispatched to the Yuebin Hotel to arrest Wang Er, but he could not be found. A document was prepared to hand over the four men and women, together with the evidence, to the bureau for interrogation.

All the employees of the Shanghai Washeng Electric Manufacturing Factory have launched a campaign to donate their salaries to help the Northeast Righteous Army. Ministry of Internal Affairs and Ministry of Finance Approve the Measures for Surveying and Reporting Disaster Losses

The Municipal Government previously drafted a plan for surveying and reporting disaster losses in this city and consulted the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Internal Affairs for review. The two ministries have now formally approved it and are specially recording it as follows: ㈠ The survey and reporting of disaster losses in each district of this city shall be handled in accordance with the regulations promulgated by the ministry in addition to the provisions of these measures. ㈡ Disaster losses as referred to in these measures include waterlogging, drought, wind, hail, insect damage and other disasters, as well as any tax reductions due to various disasters. ㈢ In the event of a disaster loss in each district, the municipal councilor of the district shall report it to the Social Affairs Bureau within the prescribed time limit. ㈣ The reporting date for the aforementioned disaster, except for those caused by sudden and rapid changes, shall be limited to the day before the Beginning of Autumn for summer disasters and the day before the Beginning of Winter for autumn disasters. ㈤ After receiving the report from the municipal councilor on the disaster situation in the district, the Social Affairs Bureau shall immediately notify the Finance Bureau and the Land Bureau to send personnel to conduct a joint survey to determine the extent of the disaster. ㈥ The extent of the disaster is classified as follows: Grade A is for damages of 60% or more, Grade B is for damages of 50% or more, and Grade C is for damages of less than 50%. Grade A shall be exempted from 30% to 50% of the tax, Grade B shall be exempted from 10% to 25% of the field tax, and Grade C shall be exempted from 0.5% to 10% of the field tax. ㈦ The above reduction in tax points shall be determined jointly by the Social Affairs, Finance and Land Bureaus depending on the severity of the disaster. ㈧ The Land Bureau shall prepare a register of the disaster-stricken fields and the number of tax extinctions in accordance with the determined tax reduction points, and shall, together with the Finance and Social Affairs Bureaus, verify and add seals to three copies and submit them to the Municipal Government for review and transfer to the Ministry of Internal Affairs and the Ministry of Finance for submission and approval. ㈨ Regardless of political tax, surtax, municipal expenses and handling fees, the exemption of field tax must be uniformly exempted according to the exempted points. ㈩ The remaining field tax after exemption will no longer be collected on a yearly basis, but will still be levied in the current year. If the levy is made before the disaster is approved and the exemption cannot be made, it may be offset in the following year. ㈩㈠ If there are any matters not covered by these measures, the Ministry may be consulted for amendment at any time. ㈩㈡ These measures shall be implemented from the date of promulgation by the Municipal Government.

New Plan for the General Radio Station

The renovation project of the Central Receiving and Transmitting Room of the Shanghai General Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications on Minquan Road has been completed. A belt conveyor is installed next to the report machine. All telegrams sent from other places are received by the station and placed on this belt, which can be transmitted and delivered by the report messenger in an instant. In the past, the telegrams submitted by local merchants to the station were sent from the bottom floor to the fourth floor by manpower. Now, light-weight reporting pipes are used for pneumatic wheel delivery, which only takes a few seconds. The old manpower transmission methods often resulted in accumulation or errors, all of which can be avoided and are extremely fast. As a result, the business aspect has developed very well. Recently, the station has been actively carrying out a new general station plan in order to concentrate all the transmitting stations in one place for easy management. The plan will be realized soon.

In order to facilitate the senders, the station has complied with the requests of various circles, and all the fourth receiving and sending branches in the Shanghai Bank Branch on Minquan Road (the general receiving and sending office east of the Old North Gate Tram Station) and the Xiaodongmen Dongmen Road, and the second receiving and sending branch in the Shanghai Bank Branch in Hongkou, now all receive and send Hong Kong telegrams. Senders can submit them nearby without having to travel far, so they are all called convenient. Moreover, all the sub-receiving and sending offices and the general station use telegram machines to transmit telegrams, so it is even faster.

The Housing Association's Proposals on Water Prices

Adopting Both Fundamental and Transitional Solutions

Since the water prices in the Public Concession were calculated based on the meter readings, they have exceeded the original prices by as much as ten times. Therefore, the Housing Association has repeatedly protested and refused to pay. Now, someone has stepped in to mediate, and representatives from the Public Works Department, the Water Company, and the Housing Association are negotiating to find a solution. It is heard that both the Housing Association and the Water Company have submitted written statements. The following is a survey of the Housing Association's proposals on water prices: ㈠ Fundamental Solutions: (A) Convert the Water Company's capital to a silver standard and hire Chinese and foreign experts to re-estimate it. In the future, the interest rate will also be based on the silver standard. (B) Water is a necessity of life, and the Water Company has exclusive rights, which is different from ordinary businesses. In addition to the interest rate, no dividends should be distributed. (C) Each user should have a water meter installed, and the installation cost should be borne by the company. (D) In the future, the water bill should be collected directly from the user by the company. The landlord should deduct 7.5% from the rent. (E) Water prices should be stipulated separately according to the user's level, with first-class Western-style houses being the highest, and so on, with fifth-class Chinese-style houses being the lowest. The minimum standard should not exceed the current water bill calculated based on the rent. (F) The above-mentioned tiered water prices should be fairly stipulated by experts from the Public Works Department, the Water Company, and the Association. (G) The contract signed by the Public Works Department and the Water Company in 1992 and the recent meter installation contract are now obviously not applicable and should be amended separately based on the facts. ㈡ Transitional Solutions: (A) Before the various fundamental solutions are completed, the water bill will still be calculated based on 7.5% of the rent. If the exchange rate reaches two shillings, it will be re-evaluated. (B) Before the various fundamental solutions are completed, the water bill will still be collected and remitted by the owners. (C) The duration of this transitional solution should be at least two years so that residents can thoroughly understand.

The Taxpayers' Association Again Asks the Public Works Department to Reconsider the Telephone Price Increase Case

The Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association yesterday sent a letter to the General Manager of the Public Works Department of the Public Concession, saying: Dear Sir, According to the letter from accountant Bei Zuyi, the telephone is a public utility, and its price rate should be determined according to the social and economic conditions. It goes without saying. Now, the Shanghai Telephone Company disregards everything and rashly increases the price, causing criticism from the public. The company is still stubbornly doing so without any awareness. Reading a letter from Mr. An Sheng to the General Manager of the Bureau published in the Public Works Department Gazette further proves the Bureau's negligence. Mr. An Sheng's proposal to increase the telephone price rate was based on the social and economic conditions at that time in 1929. If there were no obstacles at that time, it would have been implemented with all efforts. Since the proposal was not immediately implemented at that time, the proposal has lost its timeliness and must be reconsidered before a plan can be determined. Moreover, after a delay of three years and a great economic panic, how can the old case be re-proposed and rashly passed? The undersigned believes that the current telephone price increase is not in line with the current social and economic situation. Regardless of whether the telephone company's service can be satisfactory, there is indeed a need to increase the price rate. In short, the Public Works Department's only knowing the interests of the telephone company and disregarding the suitability of the social economy is indeed a cause for suspicion for the undersigned. As the representative of the Chinese taxpayers, the Association cannot ignore the taxpayers and allow the Public Works Department to act hastily, affecting all taxpayers in Shanghai. It is earnestly requested that effective methods be used to fight for a reconsideration of the telephone price rate from the Public Works Department to obtain a fair method that takes into account both parties. This plan must be reviewed by your Association and deemed suitable for the current social and economic situation before it can be implemented. For the sake of social and economic stability and the love of the Public Works Department and the telephone company, the undersigned has to speak his mind. Therefore, a letter is specially sent for your reference and reasonable efforts. The goal will not be achieved and the society will be fortunate. The Association checked that the telephone price increase is not in line with the economic conditions of social decline after the Japanese army disturbed Shanghai. It has repeatedly sent letters to your General Council requesting the Board of Directors to reconsider the case. Now, according to the previous situation, another letter is sent for your reference and joint handling.

The Cotton Cloth Industry, Sugar Industry, Woolen Cloth Industry, New Medicine Industry, Silk Industry, Ash Industry, Intestine Industry, and other trade associations sent a letter to Customs Commissioner Luo yesterday, saying: Dear Sir, Since the establishment of the customs office in Shanghai, all customs commissioners have been able to take into account both customs regulations and commercial conditions, so the official and commercial parties have been in harmony. Unfortunately, various accidents have occurred recently, such as privately changing labels, misinterpreting the Suzhou-Hangzhou shipping regulations, detaining and punishing private boats carrying goods without being towed by steamships, and exercising the power of anti-smuggling not in the customs port but breaking into shops for large-scale searches and arbitrarily imposing fines. All of these are unprecedented since the establishment of the Customs. Since the Deputy Customs Commissioner is a member of your Customs Commissioner, you have a responsibility to report the illegal practices and harm to merchants during his term of office. You should truthfully report to the superior official for removal and punishment in order to show fairness and harmonize public opinion. Sincerely, Jianghai Customs Commissioner Luo.

The Transshipment and Customs Broker Association Requests Reform of the Customs' Harsh Regulations

Yesterday Submitted to the Customs Administration's Tax Department

A Letter to the Chamber of Commerce Requesting Assistance

The Municipal Transshipment and Customs Broker Association, previously subjected to various oppressive measures by the Jianghai Customs and fined for any incident, convened a general meeting of all members. Yesterday, it collected all facts regarding harsh fines and regulations, compiled them into a detailed report, and sent a letter to the Jianghai Customs Tax Department requesting thorough reform. It also sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce requesting assistance, submitting a formal petition to the Customs Administration requesting immediate instructions to the Jianghai Customs Tax Department to improve the situation and alleviate the merchants' difficulties. The submitted letters are excerpted below:

Petition to the Customs Administration: Regarding a Petition. It is humbly submitted that while the state establishes customs to collect taxes, commerce is the source of tax revenue. It seems that those responsible for collecting taxes should embody consideration for merchants' difficulties while enforcing the law, so that the state can be enriched above and the merchants are not harmed below, and the tax revenue will also be substantial. I have observed that since the Jianghai Customs issued new management regulations, there have been many unexpected and harsh demands on our industry. Frankly speaking, fines have become the standard. However, it is not known that our industry acts as a link in indirect tax payment on behalf of customers. Although taxes come from various merchants, the losses are borne by our industry. Moreover, the capital is limited and the profits are meager, how can we withstand such unlimited destruction? Therefore, my colleagues have come to the association to complain. Our association has repeatedly relayed the situation to the Tax Department, requesting them to consider the difficulties of merchants and improve treatment. However, they remain stubborn as ever, and even intensify their actions. If this continues, our industry will have no place to stand. Therefore, the facts of the harsh fines and regulations of Jianghai Customs are compiled one by one into a formal petition. I humbly request your examination and approval, and grant an order to the Jianghai Customs Tax Department to thoroughly improve the situation in order to alleviate the difficulties of merchants. This would be truly virtuous and convenient. Respectfully submitted. (The letter to the Jianghai Customs Tax Department regarding fines is omitted).

Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce: Respected Sirs, Recently, I read in the newspaper that your esteemed Chamber has specially sent Commissioners Lu and Luo to Beijing to submit petitions to various ministries and departments regarding the bizarre actions of the Jianghai Customs' tax administration. After hearing this, I am deeply moved. However, I have observed that since the Customs became independent in terms of tariff, the various mistakes in its facilities and the arrogance of customs officials have become increasingly serious. Those who suffer directly and most deeply are only our customs brokerage industry. Furthermore, our industry is the link for receiving taxes. Therefore, when the Customs issued new regulations for managing customs brokers last year, none of them were meant to prevent our industry from engaging in malpractice. Our association believed that the regulations were too harsh and repeatedly requested modifications, but all requests were denied. In the end, because it concerns the livelihood of our colleagues, and the law is intended for those who violate it, what is there to fear if the conduct is proper? Therefore, our industry has no choice but to comply with the regulations. However, customs officers regard our industry as easy to bully and exert their oppressive methods. Regardless of the size of the matter or the rights and wrongs, fines are the prerequisite. Among my colleagues, those who prioritize their livelihood either do not argue over small matters or, because the goods have already been declared, if there is any negotiation, all procedures will be delayed, resulting in losses even greater than the fines. They have no choice but to endure it without speaking out. However, they have intensified their actions to the point where our industry will have no place to stand. This is intolerable! Therefore, on October 31st, our association convened a general meeting of all members, collected all the harsh fines and regulations imposed by the Customs, and compiled them one by one into a report requesting the Customs Administration and the Jianghai Customs Tax Department to thoroughly improve the situation. Therefore, this letter is specially addressed to your esteemed Chamber, requesting your full assistance so as to achieve the goal of improvement and alleviate the suffering. I believe that the leaders of your esteemed Chamber share the joys and sorrows of all merchants and will not regard this as an irrelevant matter.

Railway Authorities Deny the Incident of Derailment in Qishuyan

Only a Slight Collision Due to Improperly Installed Iron Chains

Regarding the rumor that a freight train on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway derailed in Qishuyan, a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency met with railway authorities yesterday. According to them, the derailment reported in the news is not accurate. When the freight train No. 494 arrived in Qishuyan that day, the iron chains connecting the cars were not properly installed during the transfer, resulting in a slight collision, but there was no obstruction. The so-called derailment is just a rumor, and the roadbed and other things were not damaged in the slightest.

The workers in the machinery department workshop of the French Concession Water and Electricity Company went on strike the day before yesterday afternoon because their request for regular holidays was rejected by the foreman. The political department of the French Concession Police Department intervened to mediate. By the evening, the foreman agreed to follow the old practice of giving holidays on the 9th, but the wages for the workers' strike period had to be deducted. All the workers believed that the company was at fault for violating the old practice and refused to have their wages deducted. The police station persuaded the workers to agree to resume work on the 9th. All the workers entered the factory yesterday morning, and took their holiday in the afternoon as usual.

County Security Corps Proclamation Clarifies Rumors

Prevent Bandit Troubles and Protect the Peace of the Village

Arrive at the Designated Place on Time to Receive Training

The Shanghai County Security Corps issued a proclamation yesterday, stating: "Following the provincial order to organize and train the Security Corps, the original intention was to guide the people to organize systematic self-defense groups to cultivate self-defense capabilities in order to prevent bandit troubles and protect the peace of the village. The good intentions have been clearly announced by the government. Now, the special training class has been completed and the trainees will be dispatched to various districts to inspect the trainees and start universal training. However, there are unscrupulous people fabricating rumors to deceive the people. The ignorant villagers are suspicious and reluctant to move forward. This hinders progress and is regrettable. In addition to ordering the county public security bureaus to pay attention to investigating and arresting the rumor-mongers, this proclamation is hereby issued for all residents of the county to be aware. Know that this training of the Corps is originally to cultivate everyone's self-defense capabilities and bear the responsibility of self-defense in their hometown. The training period is only during the annual agricultural completion, with two or three hours of training per day, which does not hinder everyone's original profession. All trainees who have been enlisted must follow the notification of the squad leader and arrive at the designated place on time to receive training. Do not lightly believe rumors and hesitate to move forward, lest you be detained and fined. If there are still rumor-mongers causing trouble, they will be arrested immediately without leniency. Do not say that you were not warned."

Collision Between Chinese and British Warships in the Huangpu River

Investigating the Issue of Responsibility

After the British aircraft carrier HMS Hermes sailed to Hong Kong, the gunboat HMS Cricket was transferred to Shanghai and anchored in the Huangpu River off the French Concession. Rear Admiral Kelly, commander of the British naval forces stationed in China, had already left Shanghai on the 7th of this month aboard his flagship HMS Cornflower for Hong Kong. At around 1 pm yesterday, the Chinese merchant ship Anxing was entering Shanghai from Wusong. When the ship reached the river in front of the French Concession, the ship was washed by the tide. Also, because the driver could not control it, the bow of the Anxing suddenly crashed into the outer hull of the British gunboat HMS Cricket, which was anchored in the river. The British warship could not avoid the collision because it was anchored in the river. Both the Anxing and the British warship were damaged to an unknown extent. After the incident, the shipowner and captain reported to the customs harbor master, who sent personnel to investigate and inquire about the responsibility for the incident.

The plan was unsuccessful and they were arrested

Some jewelry was pledged at Dehe Silver Shop at No. 124 Dama Road in the French Concession. Detectives checked with the silver shop, which said that all the jewelry had been melted, and only the bill was copied and brought back. It was also stated that the police had confirmed that Zhou Liangyuan, Yao Guoliang, and Xue Lianzhang, three of the defendants, were not related to the case and should be released first. The guns, bullets, clothing, and the receipt from the pawn shop were presented for inspection. Xue Lianzhang and others hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend them. Judge Zhao questioned each defendant about their age and origin. Because the number of defendants in this case was large and the case was complicated, the hearing could not be completed in the morning, so the judge ordered a special hearing at a later date. Each defendant was returned to custody separately. Zhou Liangyuan, Yao Guoliang, Xue Lianzhang, and other three were allowed to be released.

Why Must You Die If You Fail to Join the Army?

Ge Zhuxiang has Aspirations?

The Day to Serve the Country is Long

At around 9 pm the night before last, a young man named Ge Zhuxiang went alone to the Jiangtian Wharf in the Sixteenth Bund and took a ferry to Pudong. Near Lan Nidu, he suddenly jumped into the river to commit suicide. His body floated with the tide to the dock. A guard rescued him and took him to the Third District Police Station. According to the interrogation by Director Zhang, his name is Ge Zhuxiang, 18 years old, from Shaoxing, and he is an apprentice at the Xinda Customs Brokerage Firm on Yongan Street in the French Concession. Since the September 18th Incident in the Northeast, he has long wanted to join the Volunteer Army to kill the enemy, but due to various reasons, his wish has not been fulfilled. Recently, he entrusted a friend to buy military uniforms, but he was cheated out of five yuan and did not return. He wanted to save the country but was hindered in every way. It is better to die to repay the country. According to the confession, the director immediately sent police to summon the manager of the firm, Yang Huaitang, to the district. Yang claimed that he had searched Ge's drawer and found twelve letters of farewell. The director then ordered him to accompany Ge and supervise him to avoid another suicide attempt.

Investigation of a Strange Murder Case

The Man and Woman are Likely Servants

In the pavilion room of the house of Ms. Lu Hou, a Nanjing native, at No. 13 Shude Lane, Xujiahui, Shanghai, a man and a woman rented the room. After renting, the woman was strangled to death in the bed that night, and the man escaped. All the details have been reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday, Director Liu of the Second Section of the Sixth District ordered Xu Jianyu, the sixth Tudi Bao in the 28th Bao, to report to the local court for an autopsy. When the prosecutor and others arrived for the autopsy, Ms. Lu Li, the daughter-in-law of Lu Hou, and others stated that on the morning of the 7th of this month, a man wearing a blue cloth gown came to rent the room, claiming that he was a teacher at Nanyang Middle School. At 5:30 pm, he came with a woman, also wearing blue cloth clothes, who was said to be his wife. The only things they brought were a palm canopy and two cotton quilts. After arriving, the woman even washed rice and cooked dinner in a foreign stove. There were no signs of anything unusual. When asked about the rent, they said they would pay tomorrow. The next morning, the pavilion room was not opened, and they didn't know why. So, in the middle of the day, they knocked on the door to ask for the rent and found that the woman was dead, lying on the bed. After the judges and others confirmed that the female corpse was about 30 years old and was strangled to death with a rope, they ordered the collection of evidence and the arrest of the murderer. However, the judges examined the deceased and, according to the second landlord, the man's clothing was not that of an intellectual, but rather the shape of lower-class servants. Therefore, the investigation of the deceased's family is also underway.

Special Item

Fourth Volume of Judge Feetham's Report on the Conditions of the Shanghai International Settlement (18)

41. Municipal Councilors Shall Not Initiate or Vote on Matters in Which They or Their Partners Have a Pecuniary Interest.

(1) No Municipal Councilor shall sit, participate in the discussion, or vote in any meeting of the Municipal Council or any committee of the Municipal Council when the appropriation of Municipal Funds, or the purchase of land, the seeking of rights, the issuance of licenses, various commercial negotiations, commercial transactions, the design of negotiations, any planning issues, or legal proceedings are being discussed or voted upon, if the matter under discussion or voting is related to any Municipal Councilor himself, his relative, his partner, or the employer of himself or his partner, or any person for whom he or his partner is a lawyer or agent, having any direct or indirect pecuniary interest.

Any Municipal Councilor who is convicted of violating the provisions of this section shall be liable to a fine of up to fifty pounds. The court that convicts the Municipal Councilor may remove him from his position as a Municipal Councilor without replacement, but if it is proven that the Municipal Councilor's violation of the provisions of this section was due to error or negligence, and not due to any lack of integrity, then the court shall not issue this order.

(2) Notwithstanding any other provision of this Ordinance, no Municipal Councilor shall be prohibited from voting or discussing the following matters in the Municipal Council or any committee of the Municipal Council:

(A) Any plan to propose special taxes or

(B) Establishing a price list or its general applicable regulations or conditions regarding the supply of any items or the provision of any services by the Municipal Council within all or part of the district.

42. Municipal Councilors Shall Not Act as Agents in Courts or Committees Established by the Municipal Council.

No Municipal Councilor shall, by himself, his partner, or his employer, act as an agent or representative for any other person in the following courts or committees:

(A) Any valuation court established by the Municipal Council in accordance with the Local Authorities (Assessment) Ordinance, 1912, or any amendment thereof.

(B) Any other court or committee established by the Municipal Council to determine property tax rates by special assessment or other means, or

(C) Any committee established by the Municipal Council to consider or deal with matters related to the issuance of any licenses or certificates that the Municipal Council has the power to issue. Any Municipal Councilor who is convicted of violating the provisions of this section shall be immediately dismissed and shall be liable to a fine of up to fifty pounds.

43. Disqualification of Dismissed Municipal Councilors

Any Municipal Councilor who is dismissed in accordance with the provisions of the various sections in this table shall not be elected as a Municipal Councilor of any Municipal Government, or serve as a Justice of the Peace, or as a judge of any valuation or franchise court, for a period of three years after being dismissed.

(Note) Except for the provisions of section 38, the various sections mentioned are to disqualify any person who, under the Municipal Council or appointed by the Municipal Council, serves in any position or is in an advantageous position, or the spouse of any such person, from being elected or serving as a Municipal Councilor.

Fifth Issue Concerning the Status of Employees of the Public Works Department

A. Recommendations of the Foreign Employees Association

1. The "Shanghai Municipal Council Foreign Employees Association" is a group established with the approval of the Board of Directors, with the main purpose of safeguarding the interests of all foreign employees working in the Municipal Council. With the exception of employees serving in the Police Department, who, according to their terms of service, are not allowed to join as members, almost all foreign employees of the Municipal Council are members of the association (Note 1). The reform of the Public Concession Governance Organization Law has an impact on the status and future of foreign employees of the Municipal Council. The association has raised this issue and asked me to make recommendations.

2. Representatives of the association pointed out that most foreign employees working in the Municipal Council have a perception that the council often provides them with a kind of career in which they can dedicate their entire lives, with the expectation of receiving benefits from pensions and retirement savings. If, due to the adoption of a policy of employing Chinese staff, or due to fundamental changes in the terms of service, rather than due to any fault on the part of the foreign staff themselves, foreign staff have to leave their jobs before reaching the usual retirement age and without qualifying for a pension, the difficulties they face will be extremely significant.

3. The association then recommended that a plan be devised to protect the interests of foreign employees before the current organizational law of the Public Concession, as contained in the Land Regulations, is fundamentally reformed, resulting in adverse consequences for the status of foreign employees of the Municipal Council. This plan should be implemented as part of any new method of the proposed reform organization law, and a special committee should be established to formulate this plan. The committee should be composed of representatives from the Municipal Council and the Foreign Employees Association of the Council, as well as experts, and should include one or more Chinese members. The plan formulated by the committee should have two purposes:

(1) To guarantee as much as possible that foreign employees who are still employed by the Municipal Council on the date of implementing any fundamental reform of the organizational law of the Public Concession will continue to hold office, and that their terms of reference, in terms of remuneration and benefits, and in terms of status and promotion, will be the same as those previously enjoyed.

(2) It should be stipulated how to give full remuneration to foreign employees who are dismissed before the expiration of their expected continued service as a direct or indirect result of organizational law reform.

The association further proposed that within this plan, there should be a provision for the establishment of an arbitration committee. Any foreign employee who believes that he or she should be entitled to remuneration under the final provisions of the proposed plan should be decided by the arbitration committee, and a special fund should be pre-allocated and placed in the custody of a management committee so that the remuneration that should be given in accordance with this plan can be paid from this fund. (To be continued)

Supplement to the Shanghai Edition of the Shen Bao

Essays

Carelessly

— Fo

Six Arts of Dealing with the World!

One cannot do things carelessly, and one cannot do things carelessly. If it should be done but is not done, that is carelessness, and that is not permissible. If it should be done well but is not done well, that is carelessness, and that is not permissible. Therefore, the four characters "carelessly" are actually a morbid state of fragile and perfunctory psychology.

If we talk about the art of dealing with the world, it cannot be like this.

There are things that should be done carelessly, and things that should not be done carelessly. The ancients said, "Clear water has no big fish." They also said, "If one is not quick-eared and slow-witted, one cannot be the head of the family." These are all examples of things that cannot be done without being careless. If a person deals with the world by scheming and competing everywhere, and calculating every penny, it will be too difficult to be a person and too painful to use one's mind. Therefore, if it can be done carelessly, then do it carelessly. If it really cannot be done carelessly, then it cannot be done carelessly.

The ancients had a saying, "Be muddled on small matters, but not on big matters." This means that small matters can be done carelessly, but big matters must not be done carelessly. This statement is correct. However, it is originally a difficult question as to what should be used to distinguish between big and small matters. The words "big" and "small" are originally comparative terms, not absolute terms. For example, if matter A is originally of great importance, but encounters matter B that is of even greater importance, then matter A is small and matter B is large. If matter A is originally not big, but encounters matter B that is even smaller, then matter A is large and matter B is small. For example, the Yangzhou tax collection turmoil is of great importance to the livelihood of a county's population, and it can originally be considered a big matter. However, compared to the war between Han and Liu in Shandong Province and the war between the two Lius in Sichuan Province, then Yangzhou is a small matter, and Sichuan and Shandong are big matters. The Yangzhou affair can be done carelessly, but the Sichuan and Shandong affairs cannot be done carelessly. The Sichuan and Shandong wars are indeed of great importance to our country. However, compared to the loss of territory in Dong Province and the organization of the puppet state, then the Sichuan and Shandong incidents are still small, and the Dong Province incident is serious. The Sichuan and Shandong incidents can be done carelessly, but the Dong Province incident must not be done carelessly. Now, our country is still doing the Dong Province incident carelessly. I ask, what else cannot be passed carelessly? Carelessness is indeed an excellent way to deal with the world. Therefore, I advise everyone to be careless.

Literature and Art

Expressing Feelings

— Meng Jiao

In the past, I wrote a poem expressing my feelings, and with the support of fellow enthusiasts from home and abroad who composed poems in response, not wanting to conceal my clumsiness, I superimposed the previous rhyme.

Calling out has no plan to wake from a dream, touching my eyes, the rivers and mountains are broken. Alone at court, my heart is isolated, and I repeatedly presented letters, in anger at the times, I often tore my sword upon sharpening. I cannot bear the wind and cranes alarming the central lands, every time I face Xinting, my tears fall. When will my horse's hooves eliminate the captives, and level the three islands to vent the waves of the past?

Answering Lord Feng Shangduan's Poem Lamenting National Crisis, Using a Coincidental Rhyme

After the catastrophe, the rivers and mountains are also worth lamenting, the war marks on the sand fields are half desolate. The golden chalice is missing, I sadly turn my head, the national shame fills my chest, I vow not to forget. The sound of drums and horns are loud across the snowy ground, the bronze camel weeps in the cold twilight. Who can salvage a game half-finished? Stroking my ruler's sword, I sigh with prolonged emotion.

Science

A SIMPLE AND SATISFACTORY SNOW CREAM RECIPE

— Lushuang

As the weather turns cold, tender faces need a moisturizer. Honey and glycerin, however, are too sticky and therefore disliked by many, allowing snow cream to take the lead.

Snow cream recipes are scattered throughout cosmetic manufacturing books, but if you follow their methods, the results are often unsatisfactory. This isn't because the methods they introduce are wrong, but because they don't provide detailed instructions.

In our laboratory, during our free time, we also play around with these things. After multiple improvements and experiments, we've come up with a simple and effective method. While the product may not be as good as the top-tier products on the market, it's sufficient for winter use and very affordable. You might want to give it a try.

Prepare: 3 ounces of stearin, 6 mace of sodium carbonate, 6 mace of glycerin, 6 teacups of water, fragrance, two glass or aluminum pots, two alcohol stoves, and one glass rod.

Procedure: Once all the above items are ready, place the stearin in a pot and melt it over heat. Place the sodium carbonate and water in another pot and heat to around 90 degrees Celsius. If the stearin has completely melted at this point, gradually pour in the sodium carbonate solution (at around 90 degrees Celsius), stirring with the glass rod as you pour, and continuing to heat from below. After pouring, add the prepared glycerin, at which point it should form a snow-white paste. Heat for another quarter of an hour, ensuring the flame isn't too strong, stirring as it heats. Finally, remove from heat and place in a cool place to let it cool. Once completely cooled, add the fragrance and mix well to complete.

Note:

1. The sodium carbonate solution must be around 90 degrees Celsius or brought to a boil before being poured into the stearin.

2. The amount of glycerin and fragrance can be adjusted as desired, but they must be added after cooling.

3. The more accurate the proportions of stearin and sodium carbonate, the better.

4. If it's too dry after cooling, you can add an appropriate amount of boiling water before adding the fragrance, heating it briefly to remedy the situation.

5. All the above raw materials are available in Western pharmacies. Except for the fragrance, the other three ingredients cost about one yuan per pound, with the fragrance being relatively more expensive.

Society for Improving Social Discussions

DISCUSSING CONCUBINAGE

— Zongwen

| A Family Issue Worth Discussing |

"Concubinage" is inherently an utterly evil system in society. It's here that countless women's personalities have been degraded, and countless women's lives have been sacrificed. It is one of the heinous weapons – old etiquette – designed to dismember women. Therefore, to liberate women and grant them equal status with men in society, we must overthrow the utterly evil "concubinage system." Moreover, it is one of the evils left behind by the extended family system. Today, extended families should be abolished because the harms of extended families are too numerous to mention. How many people in society suffer from it! Therefore, the Tokyo Jiji Shinpo satirized our internal strife with the following illustration:

Republic of China

(Translation): "The League Council is approaching," Mother said. "You children must be good and not make noise! You should be polite when the old uncles of the League come!"

To prevent extended families from existing in society, we must first fundamentally solve the concubinage system! It is indeed an exceptionally cruel and inhumane matter!

The monogamous system is inherently a good marriage system. However, many men, failing to realize this, are still enamored with the idea of one wife and several concubines, truly regarding women as lacking personhood. Consequently, scenes of jealousy and rivalry, a "domestic drama," or perhaps even a "domestic tragedy," unfold within the family! Can such a family possibly have peaceful days? From morning till night, only scolding, crying, yelling, and lamenting sounds are heard. Isn't this suffering the harm of an extended family? The Shanghai Education Bureau has erected a very large sign in the City God Temple within the city, which reads: "If you want your family to be unhappy, take a concubine." It even includes colored illustrations. What a striking slogan, indeed perfectly true!

But why keep a concubine in an otherwise good family? The reasons can be categorized into three types:

(1) Satisfying one's own carnal desires: Many men, bearing the golden signboard of "There are three unfilial acts, and having no descendants is the greatest," are actually practicing concubinage to satisfy their own carnal desires. This is precisely an unfilial man using his evil "money" to insult women. His goal is not to have sons or dislike his wife, but rather to satisfy his own bestial desires! This is most prevalent in old-fashioned autocratic families, especially among Chinese warlords, such as the family of the "Dog Meat General."

(2) For the sake of sons: Some men genuinely want to have sons because the old saying of Confucius, "There are three unfilial acts, and having no descendants is the greatest," is deeply imprinted in their minds. However, his wife happens not to bear sons, so he is forced to take a concubine. The purposes are no more than four points: (1) preparing for old age, (2) wanting someone to provide for him in old age, (3) continuing the family line, (4) managing the inheritance. But this phenomenon is also more common in extended families. We often hear the phrase "marry a wife and have children." It is evident that the purpose of Chinese marriage is nothing more than having sons. Naturally, not having sons inevitably leads to taking a concubine. However, whether taking a concubine will actually result in sons is also a question. Due to space limitations, I cannot elaborate. But taking a concubine is ultimately an inhumane act. I hope that men of this type will quickly awaken. If they are anxious to have sons, practicing "adoption" or "passing on" is not necessarily impossible!

(3) Dissatisfaction with one's spouse! It's also very pitiful because, due to dissatisfaction with one's spouse, one has no choice but to privately take a concubine. This type mostly occurs under old-fashioned marriages, which are arranged by "parents' orders and matchmaker's words." Eventually, one becomes dissatisfied with their partner, but dare not formally announce a divorce. To satisfy the dryness of one's sexuality and the transgression of one's spirit, one has no choice but to practice concubinage. But this is still forgivable. These people are mostly self-aware youths forced out of suffering. Alas! Old-fashioned marriages are truly harmful! Be cautious!

But how should we remedy this concubinage system? In my humble opinion, it should be carried out in three aspects, with the following methods:

(1) Reform the extended family system and promote the nuclear family system. | This is the fundamental solution.

(2) Legal remedy | The law is to protect human rights. Since men and women are equally equal, women should have the same protection. There should be explicit provisions in the law to abolish the concubinage system. Hereafter, no man should be allowed to take a concubine; otherwise, it will be considered bigamy. In this way, I think many men would not dare to do it!

(3) Gender awareness | Men should be aware that this is an inhumane act, and women should respect their own personalities and refuse to degenerate. They should reject this type of marriage. Never covet men's money and willingly become men's slaves! Remember: "One wrong step leads to eternal regret; turning back is a hundred years too late." Never kill yourself!

Glimpses

COLD SHIVERS - RANDOM NOTES

— Wu

The autumn wind has hardened its heart and swept the ginkgo leaves, scattering them all over the ground, keeping the street cleaners busy collecting the remains of the defeated. This is truly worthy of sentimental scholars and Taoists shaking their heads and sighing, saying, "Alas! It is over now, what more can be said?"

Wealthy grandmothers occasionally give away some cold porridge and cold rice, and people praise them as "greatly compassionate." However, if a poverty-stricken ghost, driven by hunger and cold, helplessly steals three copper coins from someone to buy a sesame cake, people denounce him as "taking what is not his." The hearts of people in the world are like this, so it is truly difficult to be a poor man.

Middle-aged people most desire money, and elderly people most desire children and grandchildren. This is the common psychology of people, especially the characteristics of us Chinese.

We watch bulls fight on the wild slopes, happy and laughing, even shouting loudly. Foreigners see Chinese warlords fighting each other, happy and laughing, and they also shout loudly.

As the weather grows cold and the year draws to a close, the blood of the Northeast Volunteer Army stains the white snow crimson. Therefore, we should provide financial assistance. But there is a better and more practical way to help, and that is to join the Northeast Volunteer Army.

When life is poor and difficult, one is willing to die, but if there is even a glimmer of hope, one feels terrified of death. Therefore, praising death is always the fantasy of poets. But the cowardly survival of a subjugated official is ultimately not as good as dying for the national struggle. That is to say, the life of a dog is ultimately not as meaningful as the death of a group of ants.

A horde of heads is better than ten hordes of cannonballs; a skeleton is better than ten beauties. Therefore, good men should recognize skeletons, reject beauties, and hurl their fiery heads to the Northeast to charge and fight hand-to-hand.

Yellow makes people tired, black makes people despair, red makes people excited, and white is bland and tasteless.

MARKET NEWS

New News Regarding the Achievement Exhibition of the Republic of China Girls' School: The Republic of China Girls' School (formerly known as the Republic of China Girls' Vocational School) on Weihaiwei Road in this city has been in operation for twenty years, and its reputation and achievements have gained a considerable standing in society. It is heard that the school plans to hold an achievement exhibition in the near future to celebrate this milestone. The exhibition will showcase the artistic products and various achievements of past years, arranged one by one. Among the most valuable items are large-scale landscapes, figures, flowers, various exquisite embroidered pieces, as well as masterpieces by famous Shanghai calligraphers and painters Yu Youren, Xie Yuanhan, Wang Yiting, Yan Shenyu, Wang Huaijun, and Li Qiyun, which are included in the exhibition. The exhibition period is scheduled for November 17th and 18th, open to the public. In addition to sending out admission tickets, a lottery ticket is also attached, priced at five yuan per ticket. Purchasers can draw a lottery on the spot and redeem prizes based on the number. The lottery drawing period is set from 9:00 AM to 6:00 PM on the 20th. If you have lottery tickets, please be sure to collect them at that time. It is said that only three to four hundred tickets will be issued, and each ticket has a prize. At an extremely low price, you can obtain valuable embroidered pieces and calligraphy and paintings by famous people.

A KIND REMINDER TO CONTRIBUTORS

We are very grateful to all of you for your contributions to our publication. However, we have discovered that eight articles have been published simultaneously or sequentially in our publication and various daily newspaper supplements. Some contributors have inevitably plagiarized from other newspapers and fraudulently claimed payment. Additionally, many contributors have submitted articles to our publication, which were not published, and then resubmitted them to other newspapers, resulting in duplicate publications. This is a difficult problem. Currently, there are many newspaper supplements, as well as weekly and monthly publications. Assuming plagiarism, it is practically impossible to identify. However, this is a matter of the contributor's personal integrity and only involves a minority. The most difficult issue is submitting the same article to multiple publications. Contributors who submit articles to our publication, finding that they have not been published within two or three days, assume that the article has been rejected and is unlikely to be published, so they resubmit it to other newspapers. The pain of our editors lies in this point. Our publication does not have a fixed length, so we must publish a few more articles each day. Assuming that we find an article that can be published, we will immediately send it for typesetting. However, due to the abundance of articles, it may be sent for typesetting the next day or the day after. After typesetting, it may not be included due to space limitations. Therefore, some articles may be published five or six days later, and some may even be published ten or more days later. We must ask for your forgiveness. If we were to ask contributors to submit to only one publication and not to others, we would have no legal or logical basis for preventing other publications from publishing it if our publication could not. We want the editors to pay attention to everything and see all the newspapers, but it is difficult to manage even for young and strong individuals, let alone someone like me who is old and weak. Reluctantly, we can only ask contributors that if they see that an article has already been published in publication A, they should immediately notify publication B to avoid publishing it. This way, the problem will be reduced. We have already respectfully informed you of this method, but we have not received your understanding, and this type of situation continues to occur, which is very distressing. In the future, we hope that you will follow this method and pay extra attention. We would be most grateful.

Sincerely,

The Supplement Editorial Department
